## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the temporal evolution of a chemical species concentration, placing it firmly in chemical kinetics. The rate of change dA_dt typically depends on concentration A through reaction order laws, equilibrium driving forces, or catalytic feedback, while time t may modulate rate constants via diffusion limitations or catalyst deactivation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 (constant reaction rate independent of concentration)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate linearly proportional to reactant concentration)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- General power-law kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order dependence)
- Reversible reaction net rate: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (driving force proportional to distance from equilibrium concentration)
- Autocatalytic kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product accelerates reaction, yielding sigmoidal concentration profile)
- Mixed-order Huisgen kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (1 + c1 * A) (transition from second-order to first-order at high concentration)
- Nonlinear inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A**2) (rate suppression at high concentrations due to inhibitor or molecular crowding)
- Catalyst deactivation model: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (time-dependent rate constant due to catalyst aging or poisoning)
- Diffusion-controlled time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * t) (Smoluchowski correction for early-time diffusion limitations)
- Polynomial rate expansion: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (Taylor series approximation for complex reaction mechanisms)
- Induction/activation kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 - exp(c1 * t)) (delayed onset due to radical buildup or catalyst activation)
- Parallel reaction pathways: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first- and second-order consumption routes)
- Consecutive reaction intermediate dynamics: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) - c2 * A (net formation rate of an intermediate species in series reactions)
- Bistable oscillatory nullcline: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) * (A - c2) (cubic feedback typical in Belousov-Zhabotinsky type systems)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reaction order scaling → Power-law dependence on concentration A**n
- Approach to chemical equilibrium → Linear driving force c*(A_eq - A) or symmetric nullclines
- Sigmoidal concentration profile → Autocatalytic term A*(A0 - A) or positive feedback loops
- Diffusion-controlled initial kinetics → Inverse time modulation 1/(1 + c*t) acting on rate terms
- Catalyst deactivation or poisoning → Exponentially decaying coefficient exp(-c*t) multiplying concentration
- Competing parallel reaction pathways → Additive distinct rate terms like c1*A + c2*A**2
- Substrate inhibition at high concentration → Rational suppression factors 1/(1 + c*A**n)
- Induction period or delayed onset → Time-activated multiplicative factors (1 - exp(-c*t))
- Stoichiometric coefficient matching → Fractional or integer exponents reflecting molecularity or elementary steps
- Conservation-driven rate decay → Monotonic decrease in dA_dt as A approaches zero or equilibrium limit

The user wants me to identify which candidates are mathematically equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT).

**Ground Truth (GT) Information:**
- Equation: `-c0*sqrt(A) + c1*_w*cos(log(A + c2))`
- Numerical values: `c0 = 0.2596955894017505`, `c1 = 0.2596955894017505`, `c2 = 1.0`, `_w = 3.512949976548061`

- Variables: `t`, `A` (though `t` doesn't appear in the GT expression, it's listed as a feature variable. I should ignore `t` if it's not in the GT, or assume it's not used).
- Key components of GT:
  1. A term proportional to `sqrt(A)` (specifically `-c0 * sqrt(A)`).
  2. A term proportional to `cos(log(A + 1))` (specifically `c1 * _w * cos(log(A + c2))`).
  3. No other terms.

**Candidate Analysis Strategy:**
I need to check each candidate to see if it can be algebraically manipulated to match the form `C1 * sqrt(A) + C2 * cos(log(A + 1))` (or `sin` with phase shift, but GT has `cos`).
Wait, `cos(x)` and `sin(x)` are related by phase shift. `cos(x) = sin(x + pi/2)`. So a `sin` term inside a log argument or outside could potentially match if the phase shift is absorbed into constants.
However, the GT has `cos(log(A + 1))`.
Let's look at the structure of the candidates. Many are rational functions or sums of terms.
I need to check if the candidate simplifies to exactly `a * sqrt(A) + b * cos(log(A + 1))` or `a * sqrt(A) + b * sin(c * log(A + 1) + d)`.
Note: `cos(log(A+1))` is a specific function. `sin(c * log(A+1) + d)` can match `cos(log(A+1))` if `c=1` and `d=pi/2`. If `c` is a free constant, it can be set to 1.
So, candidates with `sin(k * log(A + 1) + phi)` are potential matches for the cosine term.
Candidates with `sqrt(A)` are potential matches for the first term.
Candidates with `A`, `A^2`, `exp(A)`, `log(A)`, `1/A`, etc., must have their coefficients set to 0 to match the GT, unless they can be combined into the required terms (which is impossible for linearly independent basis functions like `A` vs `sqrt(A)`).
